worst sheaf of corn as his offering and was not happy about the matter,
while Ada offered the best young lamb of her flock and was pleased to
serve Goddess. It is said that Ada was quite tall and strong and had her
staff as a weapon in her hand, yet she did not raise a hand to defend
herself. It is further related that Cain crushed the head of Ada with a
large stone, and the devil had appeared in the shape of a human, and had
shown him how to do this by means of illustrating the matter by taking a
rock and crushing the head of a bird.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn15" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref15" id="_ftn15"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[15]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to a legend wherein Cain, not knowing what to do with the body of his
sister Ada, carried the corpse on his back until it stank, and then
Goddess appeared and a raven showed Cain how to bury his sister. The
raven appeared with another dead raven and scratched the earth to dig a
pit to bury the dead raven in. A similar Jewish tale relates the same
story except that the raven appeared to Adam and showed Adam how to bury
the body of Ada.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn16" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref16" id="_ftn16"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[16]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
contrasts with the Old Testament story that Cain was ancestor to the
Canaanites, a tribe referred to disparagingly as being cursed for the
sins of Cain.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn17" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref17" id="_ftn17"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[17]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">That
is, vigilant to protect against corruption.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn18" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref18" id="_ftn18"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[18]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
saying “eye for eye, tooth for tooth” was actually a softening of prior
barbaric laws wherein the convicted would loose much more than the
physical harm she caused others.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>Before this, one who wrongfully caused the loss of a body part
could be sentenced to losing both eyes for the loss of an eye, many
teeth for the loss of a tooth, etc.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn19" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref19" id="_ftn19"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[19]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Formerly
“Jews and Christians.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn20" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref20" id="_ftn20"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[20]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
does not refer to the outside of a person, it refers to the color of
one’s soul.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn21" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref21" id="_ftn21"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[21]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Of
course Goddess does not do this because She is pure love and does not
take any negative actions.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn22" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref22" id="_ftn22"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[22]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Formerly,
“things which were forbidden.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn23" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref23" id="_ftn23"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[23]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Formerly,
“the Jews.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn24" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref24" id="_ftn24"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[24]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to an Arab belief that those who say the hands of God are tied up and
thus He does not help His people; and, those who say such things were
believed to enter the other side with their hands tied up to their
throats. Of course, Goddess does not do such things and She always helps
Her people when requested by them.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn25" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref25" id="_ftn25"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[25]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is a change from the original in which it said “fish from the sea”
because apparently some Arabs did not eat crab, and crab and other
animals could live in the sea and out of the sea.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn26" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref26" id="_ftn26"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[26]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
would appear that many people would badger the prophetess with all types
of questions, many of which she was not prepared to answer. In one
instance, she was asked repeatedly if one had to conduct a pilgrimage
every year, to which she replied “It would not matter, since none of you
would do it anyway,” inferring that to some questions, the answer was
either obvious or would not make anyone happy.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn27" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref27" id="_ftn27"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[27]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">These
are names give by pagan Arabs to certain camels or sheep which were
turned loose to feed and were exempted from service, as a sign of honor
to Goddess.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn28" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref28" id="_ftn28"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[28]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
particular passage was revealed when two Christian men, Tamim and Yazid,
men took a journey into Syria to trade, in company with Bodeil, a
freeman and Moslem. When they came to Damascus, Bodeil fell sick and
died; but he first wrote down a list of his effects on a piece of paper,
which he hid in his baggage, and the paper said Tamin and Yazid should
deliver his belongings to his friends in the tribe of Sahm. But Tamim
and Yazid searched his belongings, found an expensive silver vessel, and
then returned all Bodeil’s belongings to his relatives, except the
silver vessel. Of course, the relatives found the writing in the baggage
and asked Tamin and Yazid about the vessel, which they denied having.
But Tamin and Yazid were searched, the vessel was found, and then the
two men said that they had bought it from Bodeil.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Yet they could not produce a sales
receipt. They were brought before the prophetess and judged
accordingly.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn29" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref29" id="_ftn29"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[29]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Note
that this story is not from one found in the New Testament and the
synoptic gospels of Matthew, Mark, Luke and John, but it may be found in
other gospels existing about 100 to 200 CE.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn30" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref30" id="_ftn30"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[30]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is an Arab legend where Yeshua, having been asked by his disciples,
asked Goddess to send down a red table between two clouds, and it was
set before them; then Yeshua rose, made ablution, prayed and took of the
red cloth covering the table, saying, “In the name of Goddess, the best
provider of food.” What the provisions were, is disagreed upon by the
many relating or retelling this legend, but one said there were nine
cakes of bread and nine fish; another bread and meat; another, all sorts
of food except meat, another all sorts of food, except bread and meat;
another all except bread and fish, etc. But the most popular tale is
that when the cloth was removed, there was a large fish dressed and
cooked, without scales or fins, full of fat, with salt at its head,
vinegar at its tail, and around it all sorts of herbs, except leeks and
five loaves of bread, upon one of which there were olives, on the second
honey, on the third butter, on the fourth cheese, and on the fifth dried
meat. Some add that Yeshua, upon the request of some Apostles, showed
them another miracle, by restoring the fish to life and caused its
scales and fins to return to it; after which some became frightened, so
he caused it to become as before; that 1,300 men and women afflicted
with infirmities or poverty ate of the food and became satisfied, and
even after this, the fish remained whole as it was at first; then the
table flew up to heaven in the sight of everyone; everyone who had eaten
of the food were delivered of their afflictions and miseries, that this
event happened day after day for 40 days, and the table remained until
sun down each day. A further tradition is that some men were turned into
swine for disbelieving this parable and attributing it to magic, or some
were turned into swine for stealing some of the food from it but we know
Goddess does not do such things. Some say the table descended on Sunday
and that is the reason why Christians celebrate religious services on
Sunday. (This is despite the fact that Emperor Constantine of Rome set
the holy day to be on Sunday because he, as a pagan and not a Christian,
worshiped the Sun God). Others say the Christians celebrate a great
festival after this day.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn31" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref31" id="_ftn31"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[31]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is changed from the original which dictates a “grievous punishment” for
unbelievers.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn32" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref32" id="_ftn32"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[32]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is changed from the original which admonishes the people not to believe
that Yeshua or Mary are deities.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn33" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref33" id="_ftn33"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[33]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">There
is a dispute as to whether or not Yeshua actually died before he
ascended to heaven. Some believe that he was actually alive and well
before he ascended, in either ghost form or spirit form so that he did
not suffer, or he suffered very little.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn34" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref34" id="_ftn34"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[34]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Changed
from the original that decreed that people who mock religion will see
the truth when they see what horrible punishment awaits the
unbeliever.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn35" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref35" id="_ftn35"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[35]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
may be referring to the old Arab belief that the “irrational” animals,
like humans, will be judged at the end of days and they will be taken to
task for any injuries they wreaked on other animals during their
lifetimes.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn36" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref36" id="_ftn36"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[36]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">There
is an animal heaven and a people heaven, and in the people heaven, you
can make a garden to keep all your favorite pets you had while you were
on earth. When you are gone from heaven during an incarnation, the
spirits or angels on the other side look over your special pets for
you.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn37" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref37" id="_ftn37"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[37]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">In
one explanation of this passage, it is said that a group of poor or
inferior people were asking to see the prophetess, when other more
important people had been speaking with her. It is said that she refused
to turn away this group of believers, or at least the first group should
rise up and leave when the second group came, which they agreed to do.
Others say it was revealed after one of the civic leaders at Mecca was
intent on expelling the poor from the city, and the prophetess berated
them for their lack of understanding and love for all people.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn38" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref38" id="_ftn38"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[38]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">A
similar greeting might be “take care.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn39" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref39" id="_ftn39"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[39]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Old
Arab legend holds that there is a “preserved table” or a register of the
decrees of Goddess. On the other side, according to Sylvia Browne, there
is a pink marbled hall of records, preserving our charts and plans in
the most minute of details. When we are judged by ourselves, on the day
of our resurrection, we can see our mistakes as well as what we have
done that was good.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn40" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref40" id="_ftn40"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[40]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">According
to Arab legends, Azer was the mother of Sarah, and she worshiped
multiple goddesses, or the many “faces of Goddess.” Some say that Terah
was the mother of Sarah. In ancient times, Azer was the name of Mars,
later becoming the month of March. Azer later became a common name in
nobility. In the Talmud, the name of Sarah’s mother was Zarah. Azer is
derived from *iazar* or “one who is in error,” due to religious changes.
Azer was supposedly a skilled carver of statuary, or a carver of dark
and negative idols that the people could worship to bring them more
money and power, and not love. She was represented to be the first one
to make images of clay, pictures having only been made before and taught
that her statutes represented dark gods and goddesses. Her employment
was great and she was well favored by her employer, Nimrod. Some say she
was a high priestess and leader of a religious sect.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn41" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref41" id="_ftn41"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[41]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Originally
this was a discussion over the better of the two between polytheism and
monotheism.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn42" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref42" id="_ftn42"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[42]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
passage may be referring to the old worship of angels by certain Arab
religions, or the creation of the trinity. Some worshiped genii, angels,
or intermediate entities.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn43" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref43" id="_ftn43"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[43]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">That
is, the Jews and the Christians will see that you are well learned in
religion, since they do not expect such excellent work of an Arab
because they think it would be impossible for you to be well versed in
doctrines and sacred writings of many people.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn44" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref44" id="_ftn44"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[44]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
perhaps refers to the fact that some were disappointed that the
prophetess did not produce miracles, so she countered that working
miracles would not necessarily entice one to believe, since the greatest
miracle that she would ever work was to produce the Korana, a book of
light and love from Goddess, and yet not all would believe in
that.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn45" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref45" id="_ftn45"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[45]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to the fact that a true prophetess should show them an angel descend
from heaven, or raise their dead to speak with them, or have Goddess and
the angels appear to them in a body.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn46" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref46" id="_ftn46"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[46]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Obesity
is not permitted, and exercise is encouraged. To that end, men should
not tell women that certain exercise clothes are immodest, or that they
cannot exercise in them in front of others. It is more important to
exercise and make your body healthy, than to worry excessively about the
clothes you wear (or do not wear).</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn47" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref47" id="_ftn47"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[47]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
apparently refers to the Koreish, who thought there were persons among
themselves more worthy to be a prophetess.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn48" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref48" id="_ftn48"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[48]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">A
common method by which to make people turn away from an existing
religion was to tell horrid stories about that religion. In this case,
it was common to say that a competing religion was either burying its
children, esp. girls alive, or to say that the disparaged religion
resulted in sacrifice of children. There is little archaeological or
true historical evidence of any of this anywhere. Most accusations are
based upon rumors, such as was common with the burning times in the U.S.
and the demise of old folk religions.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn49" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref49" id="_ftn49"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[49]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
original word signifies fornication and avarice.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn50" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref50" id="_ftn50"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[50]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
original word referred to murder, apostasy or adultery.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn51" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref51" id="_ftn51"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[51]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">That
is, the Jews and the Christians</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn52" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref52" id="_ftn52"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[52]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Because
of the acuteness of our wit, the clearness of our understanding and our
facility of learning sciences, as it appears from our excelling in
herstory, poetry and oratory, the Jew and the Christian should not
presuppose the Arab to be illiterate or incompetent; however, it would
appear this does not matter because the world is all one people
regardless.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn53" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref53" id="_ftn53"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[53]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Sarah
was said to be a prophetess even greater than Abraham, with a tremendous
following.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn54" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref54" id="_ftn54"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[54]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is in response to the claims of other competing religions wherein one
could take on the burdens and sins of others through prayer.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn55" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref55" id="_ftn55"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[55]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
veil or partition referred to is the partition between this world and
the next one; the other side exists about three feet above our own
world, but occupies basically the same space with oceans, mountains,
forests, etc., like earth, but only more beautiful.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn56" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref56" id="_ftn56"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[56]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">See
Table B, Introduction, page x.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn57" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref57" id="_ftn57"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[57]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">As
happened to the Marianites, to whom Sally preached.</span><span
style="font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;"> These were a vicious people
that would not listen to a prophetess who preached of a loving and kind
Goddess.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn58" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref58" id="_ftn58"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[58]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
passage refers to religious customs of certain tribes that circled the
Caaba naked during pilgrimage, because they said that clothes were a
sign of disobedience to the divine.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>The prophetess believed that decent clothes were necessary, but
none that were too opulent, including those adorned with gold and
silver.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn59" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref59" id="_ftn59"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[59]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
statement was apparently made in response to certain ancient traditions;
for some groups, it was their custom to eat as little as necessary, and
some even ate foul tasting foods believing that this apparently was some
sort of merit to their souls. </span>

</div>

<div id="ftn60" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref60" id="_ftn60"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[60]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">A
genii is defined as one that is of superior knowledge and/or possesses
magical powers and they are often haughty and arrogant.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>It is said they were created of
“smokeless fire.”</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn61" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref61" id="_ftn61"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[61]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">“Wrongful
nation” should refer to those nations and their leaders who support
warmongering, oppression, torture, suppression of human rights and
liberties.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn62" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref62" id="_ftn62"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[62]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Note
the use of the rope/eye of a needle allegory, which was likely taken
from one of the myriad of gospels of Yeshua in existence at the time,
though it appears from more than one ancient text that this was a common
idiom in the east.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn63" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref63" id="_ftn63"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[63]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">So
that whatever differences or animosities there had been between them in
their lifetime, they shall now be forgotten, and they shall be granted
sincere love and kindness.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn64" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref64" id="_ftn64"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[64]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Al
Araf is the name of a wall or partition which separates heaven from
hell.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn65" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref65" id="_ftn65"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[65]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
women will be able to see the light entities by the whiteness of their
faces and the dark entities by the darkness of their faces, probably
referring to auras.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn66" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref66" id="_ftn66"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[66]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
believe that there is a special place wherein the dark entities can see
heaven to be taunted by it but they cannot enter, somewhat akin to
purgatory, rather than it being a place where the grey entities can make
a conscious choice whether to return to earth for riches and power, or
turn to Goddess in paradise.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn67" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref67" id="_ftn67"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[67]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
may also refer simply to an elevated place.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn68" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref68" id="_ftn68"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[68]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to those who were poor and illiterate, because they were often made fun
of by others, and they were often told that Goddess did not favor
them.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn69" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref69" id="_ftn69"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[69]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">That
is to wait for the promises and troubles related herein.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn70" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref70" id="_ftn70"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[70]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Note
that Goddess does not need a day of rest or Sabbath after Her six days
of creation.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn71" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref71" id="_ftn71"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[71]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Nora
was a high priestess and a prophetess.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>Nora warned her people that unless they changed their evil and
violent, warmongering ways, their land would be flooded and many people
would be wiped out.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The Eastern
Christians say that when Goddess ordered Nora to build the ark she also
directed her people to make an instrument of wood to call the people to
worship, upon which she was to strike three times every day.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>This was not just to call the works
together that were building the ark, but also to warn the believers of
the impending danger of the deluge that would destroy them if they did
not repent.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>It has been related
that the crimes of the people of Nora included: violence, corruption,
mind control and sexual slavery.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>It is also said the flood referred to was the sinking of the
continent of Atlantis.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn72" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref72" id="_ftn72"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[72]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
tribe of Ada worshiped four main deities, and not Allah or Allat, the
moon god and goddess, as the ancient Arabs did.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>They worshiped Sakia, Hafedha, Razeka
and Salema, the first supplied them with rain, the second preserved them
from danger abroad, the third provided food and the fourth provided
healing. It is told that the tribe of Ada had been also previously
punished with a three year’s drought.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>So some seventy two people were sent to the temple of Mecca to
obtain rain.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>They went to the
temple, but were so opulently entertained by the rulers that they forgot
their mission.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>A singing woman
was sent to Mecca to remind the seventy two of their mission, and she
did. The rain was not provided directly, rather three clouds appeared
over the land by the command of Evil, and the ruler was asked to select
one.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>One cloud was white, the
other red and the last one was black.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes"> 
</span>The ruler decided that the black cloud looked the biggest and
wettest, so he chose that one, but then a tempest broke out and it
destroyed the city.<span style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>The believers
were saved because they were warned about the three clouds that were to
come and to stay away from the temple on that day.<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>Those that died were the unbelievers
who came for food and entertainment, rather than listening to the
prophetess and obtaining relief from the drought for their
people.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn73" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref73" id="_ftn73"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[73]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
people of Thelma insisted upon a miracle of the prophetess. So she took
them to a temple with myriads of gods and goddesses, and told them there
was only one Goddess. The people decided that they would call upon all
the deities, and would worship the one or ones that answered back. So
calling upon all the deities, none would answer, except for the
prophetess’ camel that was heavy with young. And speaking to the camel,
it answered by immediately giving birth to a miracle calf. It is said by
some that the calf was born already weaned, or that the calf was the
same size as the mother and it would give unlimited milk to all that
would ask. When the calf drank it would never raise its head up until
all the water in the river or well was gone. But the water was
replenished for the people the very next day. Also it was said the calf
went about the town crying, “If anyone wants milk, let her come forth.”
After this the people of Thelma worshiped Goddess only.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn74" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref74" id="_ftn74"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[74]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
tribe of the people of Thelma lived first in the country of the Adaites,
but their number increased and then they moved to Hejr where they built
homes out of the sides of the mountains, which can be seen to this
day.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn75" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref75" id="_ftn75"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[75]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said that the strange camel frightened away the cattle from the
fields. Thereupon a certain rich man offered four of his strongest sons
to Kedar if he would kill the camel. Whereupon he chose one man as a
husband for one of his daughters, and killed the camel. He then killed
the calf as well. In another version of the story, when the camel was
killed, Kedar determined that the camel was indeed divine, and so he
chased after the calf to try to capture it and keep it well, but he was
not able to do this and so he disappeared regardless.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn76" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref76" id="_ftn76"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[76]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
say this was a clap of thunder, Evil claimed it was the angry voice of
Gabrielle which rent their hearts. This would have been impossible of
course, because the angels never harm anyone. Their duty is only to
protect people, not harm them. Evil also told the people that tomorrow
their faces will be yellow, the next day red and the third day black and
on the fourth day, then they would receive vengeance from Goddess. On
the fourth day, though, they were all repentant and so Goddess took pity
on them and how Evil lied to them all and so She allowed them into
paradise. Of course the prophetess told them that Goddess does not take
such evil negative actions against anyone.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn77" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref77" id="_ftn77"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[77]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
believe that this prophetess was given the power of working miracles,
though none have been recorded.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn78" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref78" id="_ftn78"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[78]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Earthquake.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn79" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref79" id="_ftn79"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[79]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Many
stories are told about this serpent; that it was hairy and it was so
large that when he opened his mouth, his jaws opened forty cubits, (a
cubit being 17-22"), when he laid his lower jaw on the ground, his upper
jaw reached to the ceiling of the palace; that Pharaoh, upon seeing this
monster come toward him, he befouled himself; that there were present
25,000 people, and when they saw the serpent, most of them died in the
crush of the crowd trying to leave the palace. </span>

</div>

<div id="ftn80" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref80" id="_ftn80"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[80]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said that she was very dark complected and when she took out her
hand, it glowed brighter than the sun. Also note in the Bible that while
it does not talk about the second miracle, it does refer to it. There
Goddess tells Miriam that if they will not believe the first sign, they
will believe the latter sign, and if they will not believe these two
signs, then Goddess directs Miriam to turn water into blood.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn81" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref81" id="_ftn81"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[81]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said that the magicians produced a large number of ropes and sticks
complexly entwined so that when the crowd saw them at a distance, they
looked just like a huge serpent and they were fooled by this
trick.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn82" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref82" id="_ftn82"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[82]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
say that Pharaoh created this horrid punishment and that he carried out
this punishment on his magicians, while others say he did not.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn83" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref83" id="_ftn83"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[83]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is told that this is what the Pharaoh did to the Israelites, to keep
them in subjection. Pharaoh came to this treatment of the Israelites as
it was revealed to him in a dream, or by the astrologers, that one of
the Israelites (Miriam) shall come to subvert his kingdom.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn84" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref84" id="_ftn84"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[84]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is said that this sign was occasioned by unusual rains which continued
eight days straight and the Nile overflowed. The rain came into their
houses, and even came up their backs and necks, but the children of
Israel had no rain in their homes. Although this plague is not mentioned
by Miriam, the plague referred to might have been either pestilence or
small pox or another plague, for the word used here, “tufan,” can
signify any of these.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn85" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref85" id="_ftn85"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[85]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Note
that “Red Sea” is a mistranslation of a Coptic idiom for “Sea of Reeds.”
(Lamas Bible).</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn86" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref86" id="_ftn86"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[86]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Said
to be Syria, which was later infiltrated by the Israelites.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn87" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref87" id="_ftn87"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[87]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to a tower which Pharaoh caused to be built for the purpose of attacking
the Goddess of Miriam.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn88" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref88" id="_ftn88"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[88]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">These
people were said to be the people of Amalek and it was said they made
images of cattle for deities, and this is where the Israelites first
learned to make images of the golden calf to worship.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn89" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref89" id="_ftn89"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[89]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is related that Miriam was told she and her brother would be given the
law, and to prepare for this favor, Miriam fasted for 30 days or the
whole month of Dhulkaada, but not liking her breath, she rubbed her
teeth with a dentifrice, and the angels told her before this her breath
was like musk, but then it was better. Then, owing to this she decided
to fast ten days more. Others say that Miriam fasted 30 days, but then
she conversed with Goddess for ten more days and could not eat
then.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn90" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref90" id="_ftn90"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[90]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Some
say that Miriam was given the law on the tenth day which is the day the
Arabs slay victims of pilgrimage at Mecca, which is the ninth and tenth
day of Dhulhajja.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn91" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref91" id="_ftn91"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[91]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Ten
commandments given to Miriam: 1) There is no other deity besides
Goddess, even though She is called by many names including male–love Her
with all your heart and soul and your neighbor as yourself; 2) Your
desire should be to make peace and not war–blessed are the peacemakers
and not the war mongers; 3) Do not associate the name of Goddess with
any negative actions or emotions; 4) Remember Her in prayer frequently;
5 )Strive to be kind and respectful to your parents, as you are able; 6)
Do not kill except in necessary self defense;<span
style="mso-spacerun:yes">  </span>7) Do not commit adultery or
promiscuity; maintain committed relationships; have one spouse only;
8)Treat prisoners fairly and do not use cruel or unusual punishment,
including capital punishment; 9) Do not give false testimony nor
volunteer testimony to hurt others; 10) Do not covet the property of
others . See p.417 for the full version, with footnotes.</span>

 

</div>

<div id="ftn92" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref92" id="_ftn92"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[92]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
may have referred to the dark planet Noir, or hell, or the desolate
dwellings of some Egyptian tribes that behave wickedly.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn93" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref93" id="_ftn93"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[93]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">In
the original story, Miriam threw down the tablets when she was quite
upset, and it is said that the tablets were all broken and taken up to
heaven except one; and this contained the advice and ordinances which
were afterwards put in the ark.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn94" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref94" id="_ftn94"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[94]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">May
refer to the Egyptian slavery of the Jews.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn95" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref95" id="_ftn95"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[95]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">By
accepting bribes in court, for corrupting the copies of the Pentateuch,
extorting usury, etc.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn96" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref96" id="_ftn96"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[96]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is referring to a story which took place in the plains of Dahia, in
India, or in a valley near Mecca when Goddess stroked the backs of Eve
and Adam and extracted from their abdomens their entire posterity, which
shall come into the world until resurrection, one generation after the
other, that these entities were assembled together in the shape of small
ants, which were given understanding, and after this in the presence of
the angels, they confessed complete dependence upon Goddess, they then
returned to the loins of their great ancestors, Eve and Adam. From this
it would appear that the doctrine of pre-existence is not unknown to the
Arabs.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn97" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref97" id="_ftn97"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[97]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is referring to a story wherein a Jewish rabbi who read the Scriptures
and determined that Goddess was going to send a prophetess at about that
time, and she was hoping she was to be the prophetess; but the Korana
prophetess declared it was she, and so the rabbi denounced the Korana
prophetess out of envy. Another story tells of a woman who read the
Scripture and was requested by some of her people to condemn the Jews,
and at first the prophetess replied, “How can you curse those that are
protected by the angels?” But after this, the woman was persuaded by
bribes to denounce the Jews and it is said that after this her tongue
fell out of her mouth down to her chest, just like a dog tongue.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn98" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref98" id="_ftn98"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[98]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Goddess
is supposed to have many excellent names, some count 99, which include
such examples as “the Magnificent One,” “the Merciful One,” “the Mighty
One”; also the Arab male prophet was denouncing the fact that women were
worshiping numerous names for goddess at that time---Allat, the Goddess
represented and remembered by the moon, or “al Uzza” from “al Aziz,” the
“Mighty One,” and “Mannat” from “Mannan” or the bountiful one, clearly
feminine deities. In fact it would appear that the oldest original name
for the Ancient Arab deity that can be carbon dated is Allat, and Allah
came much later and as a masculinization of the feminine deity. There
were numerous names for Goddess worshiped by Ancient Arabs. Of course,
this is strange that this male prophet did not know or did not
understand that the Hebrew Bible, the vast majority of the time used the
phrase “Elohim,” or “*eloah*” a feminine goddess, and “*im*” a masculine
god as the main name for god, or the “living ones” in the Bible. Elohim
was used about 2,500 times in the Old Testament. YAHWEH was clearly
masculine, but the name of the Holy Ghost and Holy Spirit is clearly
feminine in form. So why this male prophet objected to feminization of
Allat, Mannan and Aziz is not understood, other than the fact he was
simply mistaken. </span>

</div>

<div id="ftn99" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref99" id="_ftn99"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[99]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Referring
to The prophetess, because some thought that she was possessed because
she went up to Mt. Safa and then went to several tribes and said that
Goddess will show everyone that it is a mistake to worship negative
earthly idols of greed, wealth and self centeredness.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn100" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref100" id="_ftn100"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[100]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">It
is told that when Eve was big with her first child, a dark entity came
to her and asked her if she knew what was inside her, and suggested it
might be a beast. Since she did not know the answer to this question,
she was frightened, and asked Adam who knew nothing about the baby
either, and he became sad and pensive. This evil one came to her again
and pretended by his prayers said he would ask of Goddess that she would
be safely delivered of a son in Adam’s likeness provided she called it
Abdalhareth, or servant of Al Hareth, which was the devil’s name in
heaven instead of Abdallah, or servant of God. The proposal was agreed
to, but when the baby was born, upon its being named Abdalhareth, it
died. Some say the story must be false because Eve and Adam would have
never done such a thing, for they were both prophetess and prophet.
Moreover, the Aramaic name for Cain, “tiller of the soil” or Obedadamah,
is quite close to Abdalhareth.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn101" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref101" id="_ftn101"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[101]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
chapter was written during disputes regarding the division of spoils
taken at the battle of Bedr, between the young and the old. The young
did the fighting while the old stayed behind. The young people insisted
on the entire spoil, while the older ones reminded everyone that they
were not there for wealth or greed. To end the dispute, the prophetess
said the costs of the battle must be repaid and the rest returned to the
people living or to charities serving the war victims for all
sides.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn102" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref102" id="_ftn102"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[102]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
original text refers to a battle where the army of the prophetess was
situated in dry and deep sand where their feet sank as they walked; the
enemy had command of the water. When her army fell asleep the greater
part of them were disturbed with dreams wherein the dark entities
suggested to them that they would be killed because they were cut off
from the water and also had to pray without washing. But in the night,
rain fell so plentiful it formed a little brook and supplied them with
water for all their uses and gave footing to them in the sand.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn103" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref103" id="_ftn103"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[103]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
is referring to certain sects that used to go around the Caaba naked,
both men and women, whistling and clapping and claiming to be in prayer,
that some objected to. However, a better approach would have been to
have these people take their pilgrimage separately and privately to
religious tolerance. </span>

</div>

<div id="ftn104" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref104" id="_ftn104"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[104]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">This
must be referring to other people, because a true believer would never
take persons or property by force, except in self defense or to restrain
criminals.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn105" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref105" id="_ftn105"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[105]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
reason why this title is apparent from the last verse. Some also call
this chapter Repentance. Note that this chapter does not contain the
auspicious introduction “In the name of the most Merciful Goddess,”
perhaps because the chapter is mostly contains directions and
instructions for the unbelievers.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn106" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref106" id="_ftn106"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[106]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Originally
believed to refer to the fact that the prophetess was setting a time
period of four months, after which, she would renounce all treaties with
those that did not accept her as Goddess’ apostle, and then she would
give them no peace and would evangelize ruthlessly.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn107" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref107" id="_ftn107"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[107]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Honein
was an interesting mission wherein the Prophet arrived with about 12,000
disciples to evangelize two tribes, the Hawazen and the Thakif, who only
had about 4,000 missionaries. But at the inception of the meeting,
someone called out to every one “These can never be overcome by so few,”
an act of arrogance which resulted in massive retreat during the initial
engagement, many fleeing back to their homes in Mecca, only about 3
miles away. Of course, the prophetess stayed, rallied her meager groups
which were now far less than 4,000, and they all eventually prevailed
and evangelized them all, and attributed it to Goddess.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn108" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref108" id="_ftn108"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[108]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">That
is, the enemy hid and attacked those in the valley from craggy mountain
sides, hiding themselves, yet blocking every exit, they gained a great
advantage, scaring all of the people.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn109" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref109" id="_ftn109"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[109]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">The
number of angels is said to have been eight, ten or sixteen
thousands.</span>

</div>

<div id="ftn110" style="mso-element:footnote">

<a href="#_ftnref110" id="_ftn110"><sup><span style="mso-special-character:footnote"><sup><span style="font-size:12.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:
EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA">[110]</span></sup></span></sup></a><span
style="font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:10.0pt;font-family:&quot;Maiandra GD&quot;">Changed
